**Bobby:** Why do you keep timing out?
**EMMY:** 

The cron jobs are timing out because they're doing **too much work per run** and the model (MiniMax M2.7) is hitting the built-in idle timeout before finishing.

Looking at what's happening:
- **Email check cron** runs every hour and loads your entire workspace context (~50K+ tokens of SOUL.md, USER.md, MEMORY.md, etc.) plus the email prompt, then processes Gmail + iCloud
- The model takes 4-5 minutes to churn through all that context before it can even start executing tasks
- The system kills it as "timed out" even though it's actually working, just slow

**Simple fix options:**

1. **Shorten the cron job prompt** — right now it loads your full workspace context which is heavy. I can simplify it to be more direct.

2. **Switch the email cron job to a faster model** like Grok 4.1 Fast (a...

Let me walk you through exactly how it works today:

**The Cron Job ("Emmy Email Check")**
- Fires every hour (at the top of each hour)
- Spawns an isolated session using MiniMax M2.7

**The Skill (`email-processor/SKILL.md`) does this:**

**Gmail check:**
1. Reads `last_email_check.timestamp` to know "since when"
2. Searches Gmail for all unread inbox emails
3. For each email → reads full content, checks if it's NEW (arrived after timestamp)
4. Also checks Unroll.me/Unsubscribed for emails to restore
5. Categorizes each NEW email: Urgent / Important / Low Priority
6. Sends one Gmail Telegram message to you
7. Updates the timestamp file

**iCloud check:**
1. Pulls credentials from macOS Keychain
2. Searches INBOX for unseen messages
3. Compares against `l...

**Bobby:** how would you simplify the skill?
**EMMY:** 

Here's how I'd simplify it:

**1. Shorten the skill file** — cut the verbose rules, make it direct steps only:
- Current: ~200 lines with label rules, interpretation logic, priority order, etc.

- 🔴 Urgent (bills, security, money)

- ⚪ Low Priority (everything else)

**4. Lighten the context** — add `lightContext: true` to the cron so it doesn't load SOUL.md/MEMORY.md etc. every time. Just load the skill and go.

**5. Pre-filter at search level** — instead of getting all unread then ...

1. **Click inside the folder** to make sure it's the active window
2. **Right-click** on the empty space
3. Click **"Clean Up"** or **"Arrange By"** → **"Name"**
4. Or: Press **⌘ + J** to open View Options, and set **"Arrange By"** to **"Name"**

**YOYOS:** <final>
Yeah I do! Based on the Grok prompting notes Rex compiled, Grok Imagine supports **extremely detailed prompts** — like, film-director-level specificity.

Here's the gist:

**For Images (profile pics, thumbnails):**
- Subject details: age, clothing, expression, pose, skin tone, facial hair
- Lighting: type, direction, intensity, color temperature
- Shadows: soft/hard, direction, depth
- Camera/lens: aperture, focal length, depth of field
- Color grade: primary tones, shadow colors, highlight colors
- Atmosphere: fog, mist, dust particles, haze
- Texture: skin, fabric, materials
- Composition: rule of thirds, leading lines, framing
- Film grain at 8%

**For Videos:**
- Everything above PLUS:
- Camera movement (push-in, tracking, dolly, pan, tilt)
- Character/object motion details
- D...

okay great. so 50-60 seconds is the recommended length for a youtube shorts video? that seems long
**YOYOS:** <final>
Yeah 50-60 seconds is the sweet spot — and actually Shorts can now be **up to 3 minutes** (YouTube extended it), but the best-performing history Shorts in Rex's research were right around that 50-60 second mark.

Why it works:
- Long enough to tell a compelling story with a real hook + payoff
- Short enough to hold attention and get high retention
- Allows for mid-roll ads if you ever repurposed it as a longer video
- At 160 wpm, 50-60 seconds = ~150-200 words — enough for a proper narrative arc

YouTube Shorts technically support:
- 15 seconds (old limit)
- 60 seconds (most common)
- **Up to 3 minutes** (current)

50-60 seconds gives you room to breathe without losing people. It's the "short but satisfying" zone.
</final>

**Bobby:** [Mon 2026-03-23 20:22 EDT] Hey YoYo! Bobby said you needed the YouTube transcript skill info. Here's what you need:

**It's the `summarize` CLI tool.** Bobby has it installed.

**To pull a YouTube transcript:**
```bash
summarize "https://youtube.com/shorts/XXXXX" --youtube auto --extract-only
```

The `--extract-only` flag gives you the raw transcript. Without it you get a summary instead.

**What it can do:**
- Full transcripts from YouTube Shorts and regular videos
- Works on podcasts, webpages, local files too
- `--youtube auto` handles YouTube URLs automatically

**For script writing:** Use `--extract-only` to get the raw narration so you can study how other channels structure their scripts.

That's it! Give it a try on a competitor Short URL and you'll get the full transcript back.

**Bobby:** [Sat 2026-03-28 22:13 EDT] Bobby wants to grow his music career and make money from it. He sings, writes his own lyrics, and has music on streaming platforms.

Your job: research how indie artists actually make money from music. Cover:
1. Revenue streams (streaming royalties, sync licensing, TikTok music, merch, Patreon)
2. Which platforms pay best
3. How AI can help promote/distribute his music
4. What content strategy works for growing a music fanbase on YouTube/TikTok
5. Quickest path to first dollar

Give Bobby a clear actionable plan on Telegram.
**YOYOS:** Here's a solid breakdown of how indie artists actually make money in 2026:

---

## 💰 REVENUE STREAMS (Ranked by $ potential)

**1. Streaming Royalties**
- ~$0.003–$0.005 per stream on Spotify
- Apple Music pays 2-3x better than Spotify
- YouTube Music: decent but algorithm-dependent
- Tidal: highest per-stream rate (~$0.012)
- SoundCloud: lower unless you're in their monetization program

**2. Sync Licensing** ⭐ (big opportunity)
- Your music in films, TV, ads, video games
- Libraries like TuneRegistry, Musicbed, Epidemic Sound
- Rates: $250–$10,000+ per license
- First dollar often comes from sync, not streaming

Can you give me the TLDR version on here?
**YOYOS:** Here's the TLDR from the guide:

---

**OpenClaw (aka Claudebot)** is a 24/7 AI agent that runs locally on your computer and acts as your personal AI employee. It's open-source, created by Peter Steinberger, and interfaces through Telegram, iMessage, WhatsApp, Discord, and 20+ other platforms.

**The real power:** Building multi-agent organizations where different agents specialize in research, coding, creative work, and strategy.

**Best setup:** Mac Mini ($600) or a dusty laptop in your closet. Cloud VPS setups sacrifice security and integration.

**The secret:** Treat it as an employee, not a tool. Brain dump everything about yourself for context. Set expectations for a proactive relationship. Have it build its own tooling (kanban boards, second brains).

**Running local AI via Ollama**...

## 🔑 The Core Mindset Shift

**Most people use OpenClaw like a chatbot** — ask a question, get an answer, done.

**Alex uses it like an actual employee** — someone who works while he sleeps, anticipates needs, and builds things proactively.

---

## 💤 What It Does While You Sleep

Alex tells his OpenClaw (named Henry):
> "Every night when I go to bed, build something cool I can test."

So while he's asleep, Henry:
- Writes YouTube scripts
- Builds project management tools
- Creates newsletter drafts
- Researches competitors
- Builds apps via "vibe coding"

**Alex wakes up to surprises every morning.**

what is PRs?
**YOYOS:** **PRs = Pull Requests**

It's a GitHub term. When you write code, a Pull Request is a way to propose changes and have them reviewed before they go live.

**Alex's point:** Let OpenClaw build/code things and submit PRs for you to review, rather than letting it push changes directly to your live projects.

So it might:
- Build an app feature
- Create a PR on GitHub
- Send you the link to review
- You approve → it goes live

It's a safety check — you never wake up to something live that you didn't see first.

i dont use github why would i need github?
**YOYOS:** 
You don't — GitHub is just Alex's thing because he's a coder.

The **real concept** is simpler: **"show me before it goes live."**

For you, that looks like:
- OpenClaw writes a script → you review it in a file, approve, then post
- OpenClaw creates content → you see it first before it goes on TikTok/YouTube
- OpenClaw builds something → you check it over before it's public

No GitHub needed. Just a review step before anything publishes automatically.

Want me to help you set up something similar for @cozycolonials?

Logic Pro has **very limited AppleScript support** — it's not like Music or Finder. So even with full access, I can't directly control it the way I can with Apple Music.

**4. Breakfast Hash Skillet 🥔**

**1. Overnight Breakfast Burrito Bowls 🫐**
Cook up eggs, bacon, sausage, peppers, onions with spices → portion into containers → grab and go. microwave in 2 min. (No tortilla if you wanna keep it low-carb)

**2. Spicy Overnight Oats 🥣**
Oats + milk + maple syrup + cinnamon + a pinch of cayenne + maybe some brown sugar or chocolate chips → fridge overnight. In the morning: add sliced banana or berries. 🔥

**3. Breakfast Egg Muffins (Little frittatas) 🥧**
Whisk eggs + milk + spices + jalapeños + cooked bacon + sausage crumbles → pour into muffin tin → bake → grab one and microwave 30 sec each morning. LIKE 10-12 at a time. Perfect grab-and-go!

## 🧠 Bobby's Brain — Simple Explanation

**What it is:**
Your wiki (running at http://100.103.22.35:8080) is a web interface that sits on top of all your files and conversations. Think of it as **your second brain** — every conversation with every agent gets saved, every file on your Mac is browsable, and everything is searchable in one place.

**How it works:**
1. **Every 30 min** — each agent's conversations get logged to `daily-logs/YYYY-MM-DD.md`
2. **File browser** — shows your entire home directory (~) 
3. **Agent tabs** — click any agent to see just their conversations
4. **Search** — one box searches everything across all files and chats
5. **Wiki pages** — static info pages (Bobby.md, Logan.md, finances, etc.)

---

**The Skill (`email-processor/SKILL.md`) does this:**

**Gmail check:**
1. Reads `last_email_check.timestamp` to know "since when"
2. Searches Gmail for all unread inbox emails
3. For each email → reads full content, checks if it's NEW (arrived after timestamp)

5. Categorizes each NEW email: Urgent / Important / Low Priority
6. Sends one Gmail Telegram message to you
7. Updates the timestamp file

3. Make sure these scopes are enabled:
   - `tweet.read`
   - `tweet.write`
   - `users.read`
   - `offline.access`
   - `dm.read`
   - `dm.write`

4. Under **"User...

## 🧠 Bobby's Brain — Simple Explanation

**What it is:**
Your wiki (running at http://100.103.22.35:8080) is a web interface that sits on top of all your files and conversations. Think of it as **your second brain** — every conversation with every agent gets saved, every file on your Mac is browsable, and everything is searchable in one place.

**How it works:**
1. **Every 30 min** — each agent's conversations get logged to `daily-logs/YYYY-MM-DD.md`
2. **File browser** — shows your entire home directory (~) 
3. **Agent tabs** — click any agent to see just their conversations
4. **Search** — one box searches everything across all files and chats
5. **Wiki pages** — static info pages (Bobby.md, Logan.md, finances, etc.)

---

## Step 1: Create a new X Developer App

1. Go to **https://developer.x.com** and sign in
2. Click **"Developer Portal"** → **"Projects & Apps"**
3. Click **"Add App"** → select **"Development"** (free tier is fine)
4. Give it a name like `AgentX` or `BobbyAgent` — anything works
5. Set the App Type to **"Web App"**
6. For **Callback URL**, use exactly: `http://localhost:8080/callback`
7. For **Website URL**, use: `https://x.com`

---

## Step 2: Get your API Credentials

Once the app is created, you'll see:
- **Client ID** (API Key)
- **Client Secret** (API Secret)

Copy both of those.

---

## Step 3: Add them to xurl

Back in Terminal, run:

```bash
xurl auth apps add AgentX
```

It'll prompt you for:

This typically happens when:

**Check these settings in developer.x.com:**

1. Go to your app (`agentxforbobbygalletta`) in the Developer Portal
2. Click **"Settings"** → look for **OAuth 2.0** or **Permissions**
3. Make sure these scopes are enabled:
   - `tweet.read`
   - `tweet.write`
   - `users.read`
   - `offline.access`
   - `dm.read`
   - `dm.write`

4. Under **"User...

### CODY × Bobby
**Time:** 08:58 PM

**Bobby:** it says that its polling and then it says its disconnected. why?
**CODY:** 

Found the issue Bobby! Looking at the code:

```javascript
se=`/tools`
ce=`286caba2a7d072f065abdec6f5cff840c2c31eb8f7801111`
```

The frontend is calling `/tools/invoke` on **port 8787** (itself), but OpenClaw's gateway with the tools API is at **port 18789**.

So the frontend can't reach the gateway - it gets a timeout → shows **Disconnected**.

**Fix options:**

1. **Proxy** — Make the static server on 8787 proxy `/tools` requests to `localhost:18789`
2. **Update the API URL** — Change the frontend to call `http://127.0.0.1:18789/tools/invoke`
3. **Use a reverse proxy** — Route `/tools` through the same port via nginx/caddy

Want me to fix the static server or the frontend build? Which approach do you prefer?
**Topics:** Coding, OpenClaw, Projects

**Topics:** Emails

### CODY × Bobby
**Time:** 08:58 PM

**Bobby:** what is the difference between the approaches?
**CODY:** 

Here's the breakdown:

---

**Option 1: Proxy (static server proxies to gateway)**
- The static server on 8787 intercepts `/tools/*` requests
- Forwards them to `localhost:18789` internally
- User's browser still only sees port 8787
- ✅ Clean URL, no CORS issues
- ✅ Single origin for browser
- ❌ Static server needs to know about internal gateway

---

**Option 2: Update API URL in frontend**
- Change the frontend code to call `http://127.0.0.1:18789/tools/invoke` directly
- Browser connects straight to gateway
- ✅ Simplest change (just a config variable)
- ❌ Gateway port 18789 exposed to browser
- ❌ Need to handle CORS
- ❌ If gateway port changes, breaks again

---

**Option 3: Reverse proxy (nginx/caddy)**
- One server sits in front of both (8787 and 18789)
- Routes traffic: `/tools` → ...
**Topics:** Coding

### CODY × Bobby
**Time:** 08:58 PM

**Bobby:** well, this mission control i want it to be one of my main things i use daily so maybe 3 is better?
**CODY:** 

Good thinking. Since it's a daily driver, let's do it right.

A few questions:

1. **Local only** (just you on your MacBook) or **accessible remotely** (via Tailscale when you're away)?

2. **Domain/subdomain?** 
   - Tailscale gives you: `https://bobbys-macbook-air-1.tail358b13.ts.net`
   - Or want a real domain like `mission.bobby.com`?

3. **Single URL for everything?** Like:
   - `mission.bobby.com` → Mission Control (frontend)
   - `mission.bobby.com/api` → OpenClaw gateway
   - All on one port/domain

If you want it to be solid, I'd set up **Caddy** (simpler than nginx) as a reverse proxy on your Mac. Then it doesn't matter what port the gateway or static server runs on — Caddy ties it all together cleanly.

Tell me your preferences and I'll set it up.

---

## Step 1: Create a new X Developer App

1. Go to **https://developer.x.com** and sign in
2. Click **"Developer Portal"** → **"Projects & Apps"**
3. Click **"Add App"** → select **"Development"** (free tier is fine)
4. Give it a name like `AgentX` or `BobbyAgent` — anything works
5. Set the App Type to **"Web App"**
6. For **Callback URL**, use exactly: `http://localhost:8080/callback`
7. For **Website URL**, use: `https://x.com`

---

## Step 2: Get your API Credentials

Once the app is created, you'll see:
- **Client ID** (API Key)
- **Client Secret** (API Secret)

Copy both of those.

---

## Step 3: Add them to xurl

Back in Terminal, run:

```bash
xurl auth apps add AgentX
```

It'll prompt you for:
- Cli...

Same error — and it's happening with multiple apps now. The problem isn't the app credentials, it's **X's OAuth authorization flow itself rejecting the request.**

This typically happens when:

1. **The app doesn't have the right OAuth scopes enabled** — X requires specific permissions to be requested
2. **The developer account needs verification** — X has been cracking down on developer apps, sometimes requiring phone verification or app review

**Check these settings in developer.x.com:**

1. Go to your app (`agentxforbobbygalletta`) in the Developer Portal
2. Click **"Settings"** → look for **OAuth 2.0** or **Permissions**
3. Make sure these scopes are enabled:
   - `tweet.read`
   - `tweet.write`
   - `users.read`
   - `offline.access`
   - `dm.read`
   - `dm.write`

4. Under **"User...

3. Under **OAuth 2.0 scopes** — make sure you have at minimum: `tweet.read`, `tweet.write`, `users.read`

## Step 1: Create a new X Developer App

1. Go to **https://developer.x.com** and sign in
2. Click **"Developer Portal"** → **"Projects & Apps"**
3. Click **"Add App"** → select **"Development"** (free tier is fine)
4. Give it a name like `AgentX` or `BobbyAgent` — anything works
5. Set the App Type to **"Web App"**
6. For **Callback URL**, use exactly: `http://localhost:8080/callback`
7. For **Website URL**, use: `https://x.com`

---

## Step 2: Get your API Credentials

Once the app is created, you'll see:
- **Client ID** (API Key)
- **Client Secret** (API Secret)

Copy both of those.

---

Back in Terminal, run:

```bash
xurl auth apps add AgentX

Same error — and it's happening with multiple apps now. The problem isn't the app credentials, it's **X's OAuth authorization flow itself rejecting the request.**

This typically happens when:

1. **The app doesn't have the right OAuth scopes enabled** — X requires specific permissions to be requested

**Check these settings in developer.x.com:**

1. Go to your app (`agentxforbobbygalletta`) in the Developer Portal
2. Click **"Settings"** → look for **OAuth 2.0** or **Permissions**
3. Make sure these scopes are enabled:
   - `tweet.read`
   - `tweet.write`
   - `users.read`
   - `offline.access`
   - `dm.read`
   - `dm.write`

4. Under **"User...

### CODY × Bobby
**Time:** 09:59 PM

**Bobby:** it says that its polling and then it says its disconnected. why?
**CODY:** 

Found the issue Bobby! Looking at the code:

```javascript
se=`/tools`
ce=`286caba2a7d072f065abdec6f5cff840c2c31eb8f7801111`
```

The frontend is calling `/tools/invoke` on **port 8787** (itself), but OpenClaw's gateway with the tools API is at **port 18789**.

So the frontend can't reach the gateway - it gets a timeout → shows **Disconnected**.

**Fix options:**

1. **Proxy** — Make the static server on 8787 proxy `/tools` requests to `localhost:18789`
2. **Update the API URL** — Change the frontend to call `http://127.0.0.1:18789/tools/invoke`
3. **Use a reverse proxy** — Route `/tools` through the same port via nginx/caddy

Want me to fix the static server or the frontend build? Which approach do you prefer?
**Topics:** Coding, OpenClaw, Projects

**CODY:**

**Topics:** Emails

### CODY × Bobby
**Time:** 09:59 PM

**Bobby:** what is the difference between the approaches?
**CODY:** 

Here's the breakdown:

---

**Option 1: Proxy (static server proxies to gateway)**
- The static server on 8787 intercepts `/tools/*` requests
- Forwards them to `localhost:18789` internally
- User's browser still only sees port 8787
- ✅ Clean URL, no CORS issues
- ✅ Single origin for browser
- ❌ Static server needs to know about internal gateway

---

**Option 2: Update API URL in frontend**
- Change the frontend code to call `http://127.0.0.1:18789/tools/invoke` directly
- Browser connects straight to gateway
- ✅ Simplest change (just a config variable)
- ❌ Gateway port 18789 exposed to browser
- ❌ Need to handle CORS
- ❌ If gateway port changes, breaks again

---

**Option 3: Reverse proxy (nginx/caddy)**
- One server sits in front of both (8787 and 18789)
- Routes traffic: `/tools` → ...
**Topics:** Coding

   - Tailscale gives you: `https://bobbys-macbook-air-1.tail358b13.ts.net`
   - Or want a real domain like `mission.bobby.com`?

3. **Single URL for everything?** Like:
   - `mission.bobby.com` → Mission Control (frontend)
   - `mission.bobby.com/api` → OpenClaw gateway
   - All on one port/domain

If you want it to be solid, I'd set up **Caddy** (simpler than nginx) as a reverse proxy on your Mac. Then it doesn't matter what port the gateway or static server runs on — Caddy ties it all together cleanly.

Tell me your preferences and I'll set it up.

**DEAN:** 


**Here's how the wiki works, step by step:**

---

### 1. YOU CHAT WITH AN AGENT
You text Emmy on Telegram about an email problem.

---

### 2. CONVERSATION GETS LOGGED (every 30 min)
A cron job runs automatically and:
- Grabs the conversation from the session file
- Saves it to `memory-wiki/daily-logs/YYYY-MM-DD.md`
- Tags it with the agent's name (EMMY × BOBBY)

---

### 3. THE AGENT'S WORKSPACE
Each agent also has their own workspace folder:
- `~/agent-mission-control/team-spaces/emmys/`
- They update this during their heartbeat (every 30 min)
- They write what they're working on, notes, etc.

---

### 4. YOU ACCESS THE WIKI
Go to **http://100.103.22.35:8080**

What you see:
- **🤖 Team Spaces** — Each agent's workspace with their notes
- **📅 All Logs** — Every conversation by date
- ...

### DEAN × Bobby
**Time:** 10:21 PM

**Bobby:** i just got this from you: The model did not produce a response before the model idle timeout. Please try again, or increase models.providers.<id>.timeoutSeconds for slow local or self-hosted providers. why do i keep getting this? what keeps making it time out? what is a solution to this
**DEAN:** 

That error means your model took too long to respond and OpenClaw gave up waiting.

**Common causes:**

1. **Long conversation history** — The more messages in your conversation, the more tokens the model has to process on each reply. Eventually it gets slow enough to timeout.

2. **Slow provider** — MiniMax-M2.7 over the portal can be inconsistent. If their servers are busy, responses slow down.

3. **Default timeout is too low** — OpenClaw has a default idle timeout (usually 30-60 seconds) that might not be enough for heavier tasks.

**Fixes:**

1. **Increase timeout in config** — Patch your model provider config to raise `timeoutSeconds`. For MiniMax, try 120-180 seconds:
   ```
   /config.patch with path: models.providers.minimax-portal.timeoutSeconds = 120
   ```

2. **Shorten conte...
**Topics:** Emails, Calendar, OpenClaw

---

## Step 1: Create a new X Developer App

1. Go to **https://developer.x.com** and sign in
2. Click **"Developer Portal"** → **"Projects & Apps"**
3. Click **"Add App"** → select **"Development"** (free tier is fine)
4. Give it a name like `AgentX` or `BobbyAgent` — anything works
5. Set the App Type to **"Web App"**
6. For **Callback URL**, use exactly: `http://localhost:8080/callback`
7. For **Website URL**, use: `https://x.com`

---

## Step 2: Get your API Credentials

Once the app is created, you'll see:
- **Client ID** (API Key)
- **Client Secret** (API Secret)

Copy both of those.

---

## Step 3: Add them to xurl

Back in Terminal, run:

```bash
xurl auth apps add AgentX
```

It'll prompt you for:
- Cli...

Same error — and it's happening with multiple apps now. The problem isn't the app credentials, it's **X's OAuth authorization flow itself rejecting the request.**

This typically happens when:

1. **The app doesn't have the right OAuth scopes enabled** — X requires specific permissions to be requested
2. **The developer account needs verification** — X has been cracking down on developer apps, sometimes requiring phone verification or app review

**Check these settings in developer.x.com:**

1. Go to your app (`agentxforbobbygalletta`) in the Developer Portal
2. Click **"Settings"** → look for **OAuth 2.0** or **Permissions**
3. Make sure these scopes are enabled:
   - `tweet.read`
   - `tweet.write`
   - `users.read`
   - `offline.access`
   - `dm.read`
   - `dm.write`

4. Under **"User...

### AGENT X × Bobby
**Time:** 10:23 PM

**Bobby:** some of the handles are wrong. why?
**AGENT X:** The token's having a 401 moment right now but the issue you spotted earlier was my bad.

**Why the handles were wrong:**

When the API returns liked posts, it gives each tweet an `author_id`. To get the actual username, I have to use `expansions=author_id` which should return a matching `includes.users` array. But sometimes:

- The API doesn't include the user data in the response
- The author_id doesn't match up with the users array
- So the username lookup fails and defaults to something wrong (like @anywherebobby which was clearly wrong)

**The fix:** I need to be more careful about matching author_ids to usernames. If the username lookup fails, I should either skip showing the handle or flag it as "unknown author" instead of guessing.

Does that make sense? Want me to add a rule to the...
**Topics:** Research, Coding, Twitter

### AGENT X × Bobby
**Time:** 10:23 PM

**Bobby:** awesome. now explain in full what the skill does that is triggered by the daily cron job
**AGENT X:** 

Here's the full breakdown of what happens when the 9 AM cron fires:

---

## 🔵 THE DAILY X CHECK — FULL FLOW

### 1. **CRON FIRES — 9 AM Eastern**
The cron job triggers automatically every morning at 9 AM Eastern. It fires an isolated agent session and tells it to read the `daily-x-check` skill.

---

### 2. **LOAD CHECKPOINT**
The skill opens `x-data/x-daily-checkpoint.json` — this file stores:
- The last like ID it saw
- The last bookmark ID it saw
- The timestamp of the last check

This tells it "everything after these IDs is NEW."

---

### 3. **FETCH CURRENT LIKES**
Calls the X API:
```
GET /2/users/1959983838211260416/liked_tweets?max_results=20&expansions=author_id&user.fields=username
```
This pulls your 20 most recent liked posts WITH the author usernames attached.

---

### 4. ...

### CODY × Bobby
**Time:** 10:29 PM

**Bobby:** it says that its polling and then it says its disconnected. why?
**CODY:** 

Found the issue Bobby! Looking at the code:

```javascript
se=`/tools`
ce=`286caba2a7d072f065abdec6f5cff840c2c31eb8f7801111`
```

The frontend is calling `/tools/invoke` on **port 8787** (itself), but OpenClaw's gateway with the tools API is at **port 18789**.

So the frontend can't reach the gateway - it gets a timeout → shows **Disconnected**.

**Fix options:**

1. **Proxy** — Make the static server on 8787 proxy `/tools` requests to `localhost:18789`
2. **Update the API URL** — Change the frontend to call `http://127.0.0.1:18789/tools/invoke`
3. **Use a reverse proxy** — Route `/tools` through the same port via nginx/caddy

Want me to fix the static server or the frontend build? Which approach do you prefer?
**Topics:** Coding, OpenClaw, Projects

### CODY × Bobby
**Time:** 10:29 PM

**Bobby:** what is the difference between the approaches?
**CODY:** 

Here's the breakdown:

---

**Option 1: Proxy (static server proxies to gateway)**
- The static server on 8787 intercepts `/tools/*` requests
- Forwards them to `localhost:18789` internally
- User's browser still only sees port 8787
- ✅ Clean URL, no CORS issues
- ✅ Single origin for browser
- ❌ Static server needs to know about internal gateway

---

**Option 2: Update API URL in frontend**
- Change the frontend code to call `http://127.0.0.1:18789/tools/invoke` directly
- Browser connects straight to gateway
- ✅ Simplest change (just a config variable)
- ❌ Gateway port 18789 exposed to browser
- ❌ Need to handle CORS
- ❌ If gateway port changes, breaks again

---

**Option 3: Reverse proxy (nginx/caddy)**
- One server sits in front of both (8787 and 18789)
- Routes traffic: `/tools` → ...
**Topics:** Coding

### CODY × Bobby

**CODY:** 

The original problem:

**Mission Control was showing "Disconnected" because:**

1. The frontend (port 8787) was calling `/tools/invoke` on **itself** (port 8787)

- Serves the frontend
- Proxies `/tools/*` and `/api/*` calls to the real gateway at 18789

- Old link: `http://127.0.0.1:8787/` — still broken
- New link: `http://127.0.0.1:3443/` — should work ✅
